  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380877650" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1079443-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442532375p2/1079443.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380877650?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/1079443-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142677" href="/book/show/9680830-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1079443-andrea?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1079443-andrea?shelf=in-translation">in-translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380877650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12738738396101692491">We are two peoples...two peoples...two peoples<br/>Look where the first is, and where's the other<br/>Draw the lines between them, brother<br/>--Abdel Rahman el-Abnoudi<br/><br/>Draw the lines is what Ahmed Khaled Towfik does, spinning out the distance between the super rich, who have walled themselves into elite enclosed splendour on a small stretch of Egypt's coast, and the masses sunk into a hyper-violent and bestial state of misery and filthiest poverty. A violent and moral fairytale of one possible future, and a ca</span>
  <span id="freeText12738738396101692491" style="display:none">We are two peoples...two peoples...two peoples<br />Look where the first is, and where's the other<br />Draw the lines between them, brother<br />--Abdel Rahman el-Abnoudi<br /><br />Draw the lines is what Ahmed Khaled Towfik does, spinning out the distance between the super rich, who have walled themselves into elite enclosed splendour on a small stretch of Egypt's coast, and the masses sunk into a hyper-violent and bestial state of misery and filthiest poverty. A violent and moral fairytale of one possible future, and a call to action before it is too late, and written on the eve of the Arab spring. How could it not be of interest?<br /><br />Separate from the obvious political statement that the book is making, in terms of plot, I still find the common theme of apocalypse and the retreat of human kind to a state far removed from any kind of humanity to be a terribly masculine idea, and a genre which always seems to become enamoured of its own brutal depths. Octavia Butler stands as the best contrast I think, as in <i>Parable of the Sower</i>. Not that brutality is absent from her world, but with the existence of people coming together to rescue, salvage and build something new. This might even be easier once all of the rich people have taken themselves off, who knows?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12738738396101692491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1533554342" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1533554342" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19748757-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565987304p2/19748757.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533554342?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/19748757-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/20617951">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19748757-jasmine?shelf=arabic-books">arabic-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533554342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13803133369795241447"><br/>Disclaimer: I read this book in the Arabic version not the translated one.<br/><br/>I believe this is the first Arabic novel that I have ever read. It was a good read, tough, but good. The book takes place in the year 2023 in Egypt, it states in the beginning that everything in this books is a work of fiction and any resemblance to reality is a mere coincidence.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470790291ra/19965416.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>A political fiction novel about life in Egypt published under Mubarak's regime; one must say shit like so as not to go to jail. But the truth is </span>
  <span id="freeText13803133369795241447" style="display:none"><br>Disclaimer: I read this book in the Arabic version not the translated one.<br><br>I believe this is the first Arabic novel that I have ever read. It was a good read, tough, but good. The book takes place in the year 2023 in Egypt, it states in the beginning that everything in this books is a work of fiction and any resemblance to reality is a mere coincidence.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470790291ra/19965416.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>A political fiction novel about life in Egypt published under Mubarak's regime; one must say shit like so as not to go to jail. But the truth is that this work of "fiction" still applies in Egypt until now and it's not 2008 anymore, it's 2016!!<br><br>The book is narrated by two main characters; the hunter and the prey, also know as; the poor and the rich. One could wonder, how is the poor one described as the hunter and the rich as the prey?! The answer is simple;the poor struggle to survive, the prey just waits for its death.<br><br>The book begins with "The hunter" part, and the writing almost put me off completely. I have never in my life been disgusted with words as I was while first reading this book.But as I kept on reading, I understood the need to use such words, I understood the importance of language and why we all differs in using it. The more I read, the more I felt their pain, sufferance, misery, disgust, their deep hatred toward each other and the "Utopians". The more I read, the more I understood this country.<br><br>Tawfik's usage of contrast is remarkable. As soon as I finished reading the first part - narrated by the hunter - I instantly struggled with the other narration that of the prey. I was swallowed by the horrible circumstances of the poor, their inhumane actions and then a world of Utopia was pulling me towards it!!!! This. This exactly what makes you feel every damn thing in this book, this shows you that this book is not a work of fiction. It's a tug war on your mind, urging you to think, to mentally crossover the borders and admit that this is not a work of fiction. This is the reality we have been living for the past 30 years and more, this is the reality that is still happening and no one does anything about it. It's the reality that we couldn't change, the reality we can't change... yet.<br><br>I still remember the reason Tawfik chose for that rich kid - I forgot his name - to crossover to "Wilderness" or "The poor area". It was boredom. Boredom, I believe, is the most common epidemic in Egypt at the moment, I say "I am bored" over 10 times/day. All over social media, Egyptians associate themselves with boredom. Boredom due to endless restrictions, fears and lack of means. You ask me, why was this Utopian kid bored then? He can't possibly have anything that stops him. I tell you, it was because he had it all, already! What a dumb answer, but it only fits a dumb and careless person as this utopian piece of shit. I can't respect him, he was so bored that he though of suicide as the last big adventure. Then he crossed over to the poor side, where people die involuntarily, where they struggle for clean water, clean air and a place to sleep.Misery, poorness, and injustice infiltrates all the hunters' hearts, bodies and souls. Their horrendous conditions leads that rich girl - whom I also forgot her name- to turn into one of them after spending a very short time with them. The girl develops a new language, new behaviour, and new attitude that doesn't fit a utopian. This is the beauty of contrast, it makes you see everything in high-definition. But does she develop a new understanding of the world? Does she the truth the way it really is? I don't know, her last action towards that other rich kid makes me wonder that perhaps she could represent a better future...<br><br>The book ends in a revolution (surprise!) , after a particular death. But so far so many have already died, who decides who creates the spark?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13803133369795241447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_317500957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317500957" />
    <a title="Mark Staniforth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4106933-mark-staniforth"><img alt="Mark Staniforth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335734315p2/4106933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317500957?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Staniforth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Staniforth" href="/user/show/4106933-mark-staniforth">Mark Staniforth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142677" href="/book/show/9680830-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317500957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13957412213890625013">Egypt, 2023: the nation's elite cling to a stretch of its north coast, the eponymous Utopia, fenced off and fortified by shoot-to-kill squads of ex-US marines. Over the wire exist the Others, in a broken-down, left-behind world where there is no rule of law and day-to-day life is a brutal struggle.<br/>Such a dystopian landscape is nothing new, but in Ahmed Khaled Towfik's more than capable hands it is lent a new sense of urgency, underpinned by a conceit which renders his own Utopia more chillingly </span>
  <span id="freeText13957412213890625013" style="display:none">Egypt, 2023: the nation's elite cling to a stretch of its north coast, the eponymous Utopia, fenced off and fortified by shoot-to-kill squads of ex-US marines. Over the wire exist the Others, in a broken-down, left-behind world where there is no rule of law and day-to-day life is a brutal struggle.<br />Such a dystopian landscape is nothing new, but in Ahmed Khaled Towfik's more than capable hands it is lent a new sense of urgency, underpinned by a conceit which renders his own Utopia more chillingly believable than the rest: the discovery of a new super-fuel which instantly renders the middle-east's oil reserves worthless.<br />The middle-classes have collapsed and the super-rich have fled behind gates to a community haemorrhaging wealth to the extent that almost anything is possible, and in which their offspring's only burden is the over-bearing nihilism which grows out of lives devoid of risk or thrill.<br />Utopia's teenage, nameless narrator - 'Let's not talk about names. What's the value of names when you're no different to anyone else?' - is the son of a pharmaceutical billionaire who passes his days overwhelmed with boredom:<br /><br />'What can you do in this artificial paradise? You sleep, you take drugs, you eat until food makes you sick, you vomit until you can recover the enjoyment of eating, you have sex (it's weird how you notice that boredom makes your sexual behaviour aggressive and sadistic). If you knew another way for a person to live his life, I'd be happy if you could tell me about it.'<br /><br />Utopia is a world in which even political enmity is non-existent: the narrator cannot fathom why former generations used to loathe the state of Israel. Here and now, money and status mean everything, no matter your creed. Only one pursuit remains enthrallingly off-limits: the sick, so-called sport of 'hunting', in which gangs of Utopians cross the fence to kidnap then hunt down selected Others, secure in the knowledge that they stay a mobile phone call away from being winched to safety by their always-compliant US guards. Friends have done it, hauling back hacked-off body parts as trophies. Consumed by the idea, the narrator and his sometime girlfriend hustle out of the gates, but they are bewildered by the parallel universe in which they have arrived, and it is not long before things start to go badly wrong.<br />Towfik is the author of scores of books in his homeland, and is feted as 'the Arab world's best-selling author of horror and fantasy genres.' First published in Arabic in 2009, 'Utopia' was translated by Chip Rossetti and published in English by Bloomsbury Qatar last year.<br />'Utopia' is a short, sharp, steroid-jab of a novel: perhaps not entirely ground-breaking in its global vision, but undoubtedly given added potency by its setting in lands where the class gap is at its most extreme. It is also an anything-but-ordinary addition to the notable canon of Arabic fiction translated into English, and as such is a refreshing as well as exhilarating read.<br />'Utopia' is a spectacular achievement: gory and grotesque, harsh and dark, but entirely, utterly compelling. You may be horrified, but you will struggle to avoid gulping it down in a single sitting. And afterwards, you will rest uneasily with the thought that Towfik's richly evoked world could quite easily one day come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13957412213890625013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_440326656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440326656" />
    <a title="Sam Harris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13144021-sam-harris"><img alt="Sam Harris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348597827p2/13144021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440326656?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Harris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Harris" href="/user/show/13144021-sam-harris">Sam Harris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142677" href="/book/show/9680830-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440326656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4565049771554493003">Reading Utopia by Ahmed Kaled Towfik was really an eye opening experience. The book takes its reader through the life of two children from very different circumstances in a world with a huge economic disparity. Through the vehicle of children, the author is able to communicate the horrors of an insanely cruel world while at the same time clearly illustrating in an easy way how this world came about. Going even further it is set in Egypt an area which even today is highly volatile and with which </span>
  <span id="freeText4565049771554493003" style="display:none">Reading Utopia by Ahmed Kaled Towfik was really an eye opening experience. The book takes its reader through the life of two children from very different circumstances in a world with a huge economic disparity. Through the vehicle of children, the author is able to communicate the horrors of an insanely cruel world while at the same time clearly illustrating in an easy way how this world came about. Going even further it is set in Egypt an area which even today is highly volatile and with which the Western world doesn't have much understanding. The story revolves around a boy and girl who are considered social elites in their society, but in this society being considered social elites means total separation from the poor masses. These two journey into the domain of "the Others", the people who live in constant poverty in an attempt to kidnap one of them in order to bring back to "Utopia" the upper-class area to torture. The boy and girl end up stranded and have to rely on one compassionate "Other" in order to survive.<br /><br />I found this book thrilling throughout. It gave a detailed account not only of current Egyptian civilization through the 'past' memories of the others, and the negative society that the Egyptian state is tending toward. One of the coolest ways in which it does this is through the injection of song lyrics and poem stanzas at the beginning and in the middle of chapters. These songs which alternate between songs produced by the "Utopians" known as "Orgasm Songs" which indicate the two "Utopians" tendencies towards the Utopian way of thinking and the Egyptian poet "Abdel Rahman el-Abnoudi's" poems which indicate the transition to the "Others" way of thinking. Through this the writer is able to communicate how the Utopian's perceptions change as the book progresses.<br /><br />Another way in which the author manages to communicate the horrible state in which the people of Egypt are living is through his use of children. Through using children as his characters Towfik manages to communicate the horrible nature of the situation the people are living in through the children’s open acceptance of rape and drugs. The fact that kids in the street are openly taking drugs and having sex only reveals the horrors a society in which innocence is lost. Innocence lost is a recurring theme of this book and the reader gets the underlying feeling that the Utopian's are responsible for the Other's loss of innocence.<br /><br />In total Utopia is a strong and emotionally compelling story which combines and exaggerates the worst aspects of modern society to paint a picture of a miserable future for humanity. The story warns that should humans not change their ways society will break down. This book is a great read and I would recommend it to anyone who is interested in a good science-fiction, dystopia-esque novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4565049771554493003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1118809251" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1118809251" />
    <a title="Fayrouz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24520279-fayrouz"><img alt="Fayrouz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543706434p2/24520279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1118809251?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fayrouz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fayrouz" href="/user/show/24520279-fayrouz">Fayrouz</a>

I liked how he kinda gave us a brief psychological analysis of the hunter and the prey's mentalities. the last part threw all my expectations away; it was a slap on the face reminding me of the harsh reality of the world we are living in. what I didn't really understand is the ending and why'd the hunter do that ? <div id="review_440313639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440313639" />
    <a title="Carmel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4867059-carmel"><img alt="Carmel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350228432p2/4867059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440313639?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmel" href="/user/show/4867059-carmel">Carmel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142677" href="/book/show/9680830-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440313639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13849377104455824357">Utopia is a story about a corrupt society in 2023 where the rich live in the wealthy community called "Utopia" while the poor live in vicious slums. The main character is addicted to sex and drugs, but is generally completely bored with his life, though he has everything provided for him. He decides to sneak out of Utopia with one of his girlfriends, abduct a poor person, and murder them. Through a series of events, the two characters become stuck in the slums and try to sneak back into Utopia.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText13849377104455824357" style="display:none">Utopia is a story about a corrupt society in 2023 where the rich live in the wealthy community called "Utopia" while the poor live in vicious slums. The main character is addicted to sex and drugs, but is generally completely bored with his life, though he has everything provided for him. He decides to sneak out of Utopia with one of his girlfriends, abduct a poor person, and murder them. Through a series of events, the two characters become stuck in the slums and try to sneak back into Utopia.<br /><br />This was a very powerful book, with many obvious warnings about the future and what could go wrong. I wouldn't say that I "liked" it, but the book was well-written and I would recommend it. Since the book takes place only a few years in the future, it was crazy to hear that life could change so drastically by then. The author refers to several historical events, such as past US presidents and the Iraq War, which made the story more believable and realistic. The reason that I'm giving it three stars is that I didn't like the ending at all. I can understand why the author wrote it that way, but I would have preferred something more fulfilling. In addition, I could not stand the main character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13849377104455824357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11796656890123558360">We immediately know the teenage protagonist is both debauched and depraved because he sports a purple mohawk. He takes all manner of drugs, has sex with anything that moves, thinks violence is thrilling, and has no respect for anyone or anybody -- not even his parents. He even listens to "orgasm music" which features "insane screaming" of lyrics with no redeeming social value. Horrors!<br/><br/>This city of Utopia is anything but. It's a dystopia (clever, what?) set in the near future in Egypt. Perhaps th</span>
  <span id="freeText11796656890123558360" style="display:none">We immediately know the teenage protagonist is both debauched and depraved because he sports a purple mohawk. He takes all manner of drugs, has sex with anything that moves, thinks violence is thrilling, and has no respect for anyone or anybody -- not even his parents. He even listens to "orgasm music" which features "insane screaming" of lyrics with no redeeming social value. Horrors!<br /><br />This city of Utopia is anything but. It's a dystopia (clever, what?) set in the near future in Egypt. Perhaps there's some brilliant political subtext here but if so I missed it. It seemed to me a simplistic, heavy-handed and frankly nauseating morality fable about haves and have-nots. There's nothing new here. It's depressing but not particularly artful. The air of putrid nihilism left me with the same condition as the residents of Utopia: terminal boredom.<br /><br />At least it was mercifully brief.</span>

  <span id="freeText4114018188647546719" style="display:none">There are times when I feel that rating a book with only 5☆ is unfair because they deserve more. <br />This took me back to "1984" by George Orwell but in a different way and taste. <br />both writers wrote a sort of future which we can't miss or deny now, They are both smart and have their own unique visions though here in "Utopia" things are different according to the time, the place, the actions and the people of course. <br />Ahmed Khaled Tawfik is the Egyptian Orwell.<br />whenever you read the word "Utopia" Plato is the first person hits your thoughts or the words "المدينة الفاضلة" <br />The word gives the impression of a perfect world with no sadness, worries or sins. A world when you can live happy ever after. But whoever studies philosophy knows well that Utopia isn't the place you are looking for and when you try to found this Utopia, you will be destroyed by the same concepts you fought for before to found it.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3121688837" />
    <a title="Antti Kirjavainen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44552047-antti-kirjavainen"><img alt="Antti Kirjavainen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3121688837?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antti Kirjavainen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antti Kirjavainen" href="/user/show/44552047-antti-kirjavainen">Antti Kirjavainen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789520108922" href="/book/show/17368415-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3121688837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15938970043837626028">This little book packs a mighty punch!<br/><br/>It is set in Egypt in dystopic near future, but the future it paints has facets that remind me of possible dystopic futures in our society, too. The book discusses the themes of social equity and human rights, commercialism, meaning in the modern world in a powerful and moving way.<br/><br/>At times, the story is a bit on the nose, but that fits the style of narration. I read this short book in less than a day, and the brevity added to the strength of the experience. </span>
  <span id="freeText15938970043837626028" style="display:none">This little book packs a mighty punch!<br /><br />It is set in Egypt in dystopic near future, but the future it paints has facets that remind me of possible dystopic futures in our society, too. The book discusses the themes of social equity and human rights, commercialism, meaning in the modern world in a powerful and moving way.<br /><br />At times, the story is a bit on the nose, but that fits the style of narration. I read this short book in less than a day, and the brevity added to the strength of the experience. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1483651783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1483651783" />
    <a title="Marilyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50696904-marilyn"><img alt="Marilyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498572486p2/50696904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1483651783?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marilyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marilyn" href="/user/show/50696904-marilyn">Marilyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142677" href="/book/show/9680830-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1483651783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16898543943159031919">Terrible story and terrible writing style. The author does not know how to tell a story; instead of immersing the reader, the author blatantly narrates what is happening through the characters. What you basically end up reading is a long-winded idea. The author fails to describe scenes for what they are. For example, he will tell you "it was like the scene from X movie" or "it was like the Holacaust." What he is really doing is showing off his knowledge of cultural events and objects, so that in</span>
  <span id="freeText16898543943159031919" style="display:none">Terrible story and terrible writing style. The author does not know how to tell a story; instead of immersing the reader, the author blatantly narrates what is happening through the characters. What you basically end up reading is a long-winded idea. The author fails to describe scenes for what they are. For example, he will tell you "it was like the scene from X movie" or "it was like the Holacaust." What he is really doing is showing off his knowledge of cultural events and objects, so that in effect you are reading an uncreative description told from a condescending perspective. <br /><br />The characters are very difficult to relate to -- they are either unrealistically evil, unrealistically absurd or unbelievably moral. The only role women serve are as sex objects -- either they engage in consensual sex or they are being raped. <br /><br />"Utopia" clearly embodies a conservative viewpoint by linking liberalism with selfishness. The story shallowly encourages stereotypes -- which goes against what literature is supposed to do; some stereotypes include assumptions such as that all Japanese are hardworking, all Americans are in love with war, all Egyptians are lazy, etc. <br /><br />In the end, story basically encourages hatred toward one side : the wealthy community. In my opinion, this is not literature, as it does not enlighten nor widen one's perspective. Instead, it is the thoughts of a narrow-minded, stereotyped, anger-filled perspective that proposes that the only solution is force.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16898543943159031919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2354798555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2354798555" />
    <a title="منال" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21302867"><img alt="منال" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594745541p2/21302867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2354798555?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="منال" class="user" itemprop="url" name="منال" href="/user/show/21302867">منال</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142677" href="/book/show/9680830-utopia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2354798555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6786986425428650906">After the 20 first pages of Utopia, I had started telling myself I probably had landed my eyes on the worst book Ahmad ever wrote. That maybe it was a bad choice to begin with. That there were many other options I could have taken.<br/>But you can't really judge an imaginated story based on the values it chose to unveil, or the vocabulary the author had lent to his character's conversations. Or how disgusting the personalities he imagined were. Especially when it's done on purpose.<br/>That was what motiv</span>
  <span id="freeText6786986425428650906" style="display:none">After the 20 first pages of Utopia, I had started telling myself I probably had landed my eyes on the worst book Ahmad ever wrote. That maybe it was a bad choice to begin with. That there were many other options I could have taken.<br />But you can't really judge an imaginated story based on the values it chose to unveil, or the vocabulary the author had lent to his character's conversations. Or how disgusting the personalities he imagined were. Especially when it's done on purpose.<br />That was what motivated me while I carried on reading. And I guess the way the story ended was absolutely worth it. <br />The Utopian who started off the narration, was subject to my disgust at first, A disgust that left place to amusement and finally led to pity.<br />The book finally succeeded in filling you, somehow with something. And left you to think.<br />And that's all it has to ever do.<br /><br />The coin Ahmad had shown had two sides. One was Utopians, the other, well was the 'others'.<br />The rich had the previlege of a name, identified dignified.<br />The poor were just others, whom you discovered along the pages, whose existence and life was a mystery, a source of thrill even. And whose presence in the story didn't figure in the book's name.<br />As Utopia had.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6786986425428650906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

These guys mass-produce books and in the process of doing so they seem to have mastered storytelling. One last thing: if the writer thinks that snippets of sex and drugs can turn his work into serious stuff then he must have been living his own 'utopia'.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SxO6SUoBSFGpmrR+YncuaQ2E0/wxpKP7ruFSVyO4vFVxNdOb8V+BOQ6xAB+VgiS229s0NP8pLZz1nxTm7vtOzw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BaOsaCh2LyLvtXU7zBIhQ7P2iekgRoxVuYKOqZghr14/hcW6kyjmSkiewVo75yucZaluIe7LAjLi/MgYVWJdxA==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9425286509403526085">See <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16019981.Ahmed_Khaled_Towfik' title='Ahmed Khaled Towfik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ahmed Khaled Towfik</a>.<br/>Arabic Name: أحمد خالد توفيق<br/>Finnish Transliteration: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Ahmed%20Khaled%20Tawfiq' title='Ahmed Khaled Tawfiq' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ahmed Khaled Tawfiq</a><br/><br/>أحمد خالد توفيق فراج (10 يونيو 1962 - 2 أبريل 2018)<br/>طبيب وأديب مصري، ويعتبر أول كاتب عربي في مجال أدب الرعب و الأشهر في مجال أدب الشباب والفانتازيا والخيال العلمي ويلقب بالعراب.<br/><br/>ولد بمدينة طنطا عاصمة محافظة الغربية فى اليوم العاشر من شهر يونيو عام 1962، وتخرج من كلية الطب عام 1985، كما حصل على الدكتوراة ف</span>
  <span id="freeText9425286509403526085" style="display:none">See <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16019981.Ahmed_Khaled_Towfik" title="Ahmed Khaled Towfik" rel="nofollow noopener">Ahmed Khaled Towfik</a>.<br />Arabic Name: أحمد خالد توفيق<br />Finnish Transliteration: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Ahmed%20Khaled%20Tawfiq" title="Ahmed Khaled Tawfiq" rel="nofollow noopener">Ahmed Khaled Tawfiq</a><br /><br />أحمد خالد توفيق فراج (10 يونيو 1962 - 2 أبريل 2018)<br />طبيب وأديب مصري، ويعتبر أول كاتب عربي في مجال أدب الرعب و الأشهر في مجال أدب الشباب والفانتازيا والخيال العلمي ويلقب بالعراب.<br /><br />ولد بمدينة طنطا عاصمة محافظة الغربية فى اليوم العاشر من شهر يونيو عام 1962، وتخرج من كلية الطب عام 1985، كما حصل على الدكتوراة فى طب المناطق الحارة عام 1997. متزوج من د. منال أخصائية صدر في كلية طب طنطا – وهي من المنوفية - ولديه من الأبناء (محمد) و(مريم).<br /><br />بدأ أحمد خالد العمل فى المؤسسة العربية الحديثة عام 1992 ككاتب رعب لسلسلة (ما وراء الطبيعة) حيث تقدم بأولى رواياته (أسطورة مصاص الدماء) ولم تلق في البدء قبولاً في المؤسسة. حيث نصحه أحد المسئولين هناك في المؤسسة أن يدعه من ذلك ويكتب (بوليسي) وأنه لابد له فعلاً أن يكتب (بوليصي) - كما نطقها - لكن مسئول آخر هناك هو أحمد المقدم اقتنع بالفكرة التي تقتضي بأن أدب الرعب ليس منتشراً وقد ينجح لأنه لونٌ جديد .. ورتب له مقابلة مع الأستاذ حمدي مصطفى مدير المؤسسة الذي قابله ببشاشة، وأخبره أنه سيكوّن لجنة لتدرس قصته. وانتظر أحمد اللجنة التي أخرجت تقريرها كالآتي: أسلوب ركيك، ومفكك، وتنقصه الحبكة الروائية، بالإضافة إلى غموض فكرة الرواية و .. و .. و أصيب بالطبع بإحباط شديد .. ولكن حمدي مصطفى أخبره أنه سيعرض القصة على لجنة أخرى وتم هذا بالفعل لتظهر النتيجة: الأسلوب ممتاز، ومترابط، به حبكة روائية، فكرة القصة واضحة، وبها إثارة وتشويق إمضاء: د. نبيل فاروق، ويقول الدكتور احمد أنه لن ينسى لنبيل أنه كان سبباً مباشراً في دخوله المؤسسة وإلا فإن د. أحمد كان بالتأكيد سيستمر في الكتابة لمدة عام آخر ثم ينسى الموضوع برمته نهائياً، لهذا فإنه يحفظ هذا الجميل لنبيل فاروق.<br /><br />يعدّ د. أحمد من الكتاب العرب النادرين الذين يكتبون في هذا المجال بمثل هذا التخصص - إن لم يكن أولهم - ( ما وراء الطبيعة ) .. تلك السلسلة التي عشقناها جميعاً ببطلها (رفعت إسماعيل) الساخر العجوز، والذى أظهر لنا د. (أحمد) عن طريقه مدى اعتزازه بعروبته، ومدى تدينه وإلتزامه وعبقريته أيضاً، بعد ذلك أخرج لنا د. (أحمد ) سلسلة (فانتازيا) الرائعة ببطلتها (عبير)، وهذه بينت لنا كم أن د. (أحمد خيالي يكره الواقع. تلتهما سلسلة (سافاري) ببطلها علاء عبد العظيم، وعرفنا من خلال تلك السلسلة المتميزة مدى حب أحمد لمهنته كطبيب، ومدى عشقه وولعه بها.<br /><br />له العديد من الكتب مع <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/54085._dar_lila" rel="nofollow noopener"> <b>دار لـيلـى</b><br />(كيان كورب) للنشر والتوزيع والطباعة </a> ترجم العشرات من الروايات الأجنبية هذا بالإضافة إلى بعض الإصدارات على الشبكة العنكبوتية. انضم في نوفمبر 2004 إلى مجلة الشباب ليكتب فيها قصصاً في صفحة ثابتة له تحت عنوان (الآن نفتح الصندوق)، كما كتب في العديد من الإصدارات الدورية كمجلة الفن السابع.<br /><br />تُوفي في 2 أبريل 2018 عن عمر يناهز 55 عامًا.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9425286509403526085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3545602">Quotes from يوتوبيا</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;قال لي سالم بيه: "أنت تقرأ كثيرا..أنت مجنون!" .. قلت له إن القراءة بالنسبة لي نوع رخيص من المخدرات. لا أفعل بها شيئاً سوى الغياب عن الوعي. في الماضي -تصور هذا- كانوا يقرءون من أجل إكتساب الوعي ! ..&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/240986">1179 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;عندما تشم الحريق ولا تنذر من حولك.. فأنت بشكل ما ساهمت فى إشعال الحريق&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
